<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The detection of primordial B-mode polarization in the CMB requires precise removal of polarized Galactic foregrounds. While ML techniques like CNNs show promise as alternative cleaning methods, their applicability to real data depends critically on generalization beyond training assumptions. Current approaches risk systematic biases due to foreground model mismatches, necessitating a systematic study of CNN generalization properties across diverse foreground scenarios.

Method: We train various CNN architectures on simulations generated from multiple Galactic foreground models with different statistical properties. We systematically evaluate generalization by testing trained networks on foreground models excluded from training. To characterize foreground complexity, we use statistical moments (variance, skewness) and Shannon entropy $H = -\sum p_i \log p_i$, establishing a hierarchy of statistical complexity among foreground models. Performance is quantified through bias and precision metrics when estimating the tensor-to-scalar ratio $r$ from cleaned maps.

Result: Training CNNs on statistically complex foreground models (higher variance, skewness, and entropy) significantly improves performance on unseen foreground variations. Networks trained on simple models exhibit systematic biases in $r$ estimation when applied to complex foregrounds, with errors exceeding statistical uncertainties. Conversely, networks trained on complex models maintain low bias and improved precision across diverse test scenarios. The statistical complexity hierarchy predicts generalization performance: training on models at or above the complexity of test data minimizes systematic errors.

Conclusion: Generalization failure represents a critical systematic uncertainty in ML-based foreground removal for CMB B-mode analysis. The statistical complexity of training foreground models directly determines CNN robustness: complex model training enables reliable application to real data with unknown foreground properties, while simplified training introduces dangerous systematic biases. This work establishes quantitative criteria (variance, skewness, entropy) for foreground model selection and emphasizes the necessity of incorporating diverse, realistic foreground scenarios in ML training pipelines for cosmological parameter estimation.

Abstract: The detection of Cosmic Microwave Background primordial $B$-mode polarization would constitute a ``smoking gun" signal of primordial gravitational waves. However, this measurement requires accurate removal of polarized Galactic foregrounds to avoid systematic biases when estimating the tensor-to-scalar ratio. Methods based on Machine Learning techniques (ML), such as Convolutional Neural Networks (CNNs), have recently been proposed as alternative foreground cleaning techniques, but their applicability to real data relies on their ability to generalize beyond the models assumed during training. In this work, we focus on a variety of foreground models (FMs) used for training and conduct a systematic study of the generalization properties of a CNN-based method. We train various CNN architectures on simulations generated from different Galactic FMs, and test their performance on models not used during the training. By characterizing the statistical properties of the FMs using variance, skewness, and Shannon entropy, we define a statistical complexity hierarchy among them. We show that training on the more complex FMs reduces bias and improves precision when testing on unseen FMs, whereas training on the simplest model could introduce systematic errors. These results evidence that a lack of generalization is a relevant source of systematic uncertainty, and emphasize the importance of understanding the impact of the models assumed during training in ML-based methods before applying them to real data.

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Interacting dark sector models allow energy-momentum exchange between CDM and DE, potentially resolving cosmological tensions. While background expansion can mimic $Λ$CDM, their perturbation evolution differs fundamentally, requiring precise nonlinear modeling for LSS tests.

Method: Derived exact evolution equations for second- and third-order kernels in IDS cosmologies without EdS approximation. Numerically solved time-dependent kernel equations to compute one-loop corrections to matter power spectrum using standard perturbation theory formalism.

Result: Found that even small dark sector interactions induce non-trivial time dependence in perturbative kernels, breaking EdS approximation. One-loop corrections exhibit percent-level deviations significantly enhanced compared to $Λ$CDM. Time-dependent kernel treatment is essential to avoid biases on mildly nonlinear scales.

Abstract: Interacting dark sector (IDS) models provide a commonly explored extension of the standard $Λ$CDM cosmology, allowing for non-gravitational energy--momentum exchange between cold dark matter (CDM) and dark energy (DE). Although such models can be constructed to reproduce the same background expansion history as $Λ$CDM, their impact on the growth of cosmic structures is fundamentally different and requires a careful treatment of cosmological perturbations. In this work, we develop the one-loop Standard Perturbation Theory (SPT) formalism for IDS cosmologies without invoking the Einstein--de~Sitter (EdS) approximation. We show that even weak dark sector interactions induce a non-trivial time dependence in the perturbative kernels, leading to a breakdown of the EdS approximation commonly assumed in $Λ$CDM analyses. By deriving and numerically solving the evolution equations for the second- and third-order kernels, we compute the corresponding one-loop corrections to the matter power spectrum and find that the resulting deviations can significantly exceed the percent level, even for small interaction strengths. Our results demonstrate that nonlinear corrections are systematically enhanced in IDS models and that neglecting the full time dependence of the kernels can lead to biased predictions on mildly nonlinear scales. These findings establish the necessity of a time-dependent perturbative treatment for IDS scenarios and provide a robust framework for precision tests using nonlinear large-scale structure (LSS) observables.

### [61] [Sound Speed Resonance in the Gravitational Wave Background as a probe for non-standard early universe cosmologies](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.12580)
*Igor de O. C. Pedreira,Amara Ilyas,Ziwei Wang,Leila L. Graef,Yi-Fu Cai*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: Analyzes how scalar-tensor extensions of gravity modify gravitational wave propagation via effective friction and propagation speed, potentially creating resonances that amplify primordial tensor modes to detectable levels for LISA/Einstein Telescope, offering new probes of early universe physics.

分析标量-张量引力扩展如何通过有效摩擦和传播速度修改引力波传播，可能产生共振将原始张量模式放大到LISA/爱因斯坦望远镜可探测的水平，为早期宇宙物理学提供新探针。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Gravitational waves serve as a powerful probe of fundamental gravity theories beyond general relativity, particularly in scalar-tensor extensions where additional degrees of freedom modify GW propagation via effective friction and propagation speed changes. These modifications may induce resonant phenomena that enhance primordial tensor modes from the early Universe to detectable levels by upcoming experiments like LISA and the Einstein Telescope, providing a unique window into fundamental physics at high energies.

引力波作为超越广义相对论的基本引力理论的有力探针，特别在标量-张量扩展中，额外的自由度通过有效摩擦和传播速度变化修改GW传播。这些修改可能产生共振现象，将来自早期宇宙的原始张量模式增强到即将进行的实验（如LISA和爱因斯坦望远镜）可探测的水平，为高能基础物理学提供独特窗口。

Method: Theoretical framework analysis of scalar-tensor gravity extensions where additional scalar fields modify the gravitational wave propagation equation: $\\square h_{\\mu\\nu} + 3H(1-\\alpha_{\\text{friction}}) \\dot{h}_{\\mu\\nu} - (c_{T}^{2}/a^{2})\\nabla^{2}h_{\\mu\\nu} = 0$, with $\\alpha_{\\text{friction}}$ characterizing friction modifications and $c_{T}$ the tensor propagation speed. Analytical study of resonant phenomena through parametric amplification when the modified friction term or propagation speed oscillates with frequencies matching background scalar field dynamics. Calculation of stochastic gravitational wave background (SBGW) spectrum enhancement: $\\Omega_{\\text{GW}}(f) = \\Omega_{\\text{GW}}^{\\text{prim}}(f) \\times \\mathcal{R}(f; \\theta_{\\text{model}}, r, n_{t})$, where $\\mathcal{R}$ is the resonance enhancement factor dependent on model parameters $\\theta_{\\text{model}}$ and primordial tensor spectrum parameters (tensor-to-scalar ratio $r$, tensor spectral index $n_{t}$).

标量-张量引力扩展的理论框架分析，其中额外的标量场修改引力波传播方程：$\\square h_{\\mu\\nu} + 3H(1-\\alpha_{\\text{friction}}) \\dot{h}_{\\mu\\nu} - (c_{T}^{2}/a^{2})\\nabla^{2}h_{\\mu\\nu} = 0$，其中$\\alpha_{\\text{friction}}$表征摩擦修正，$c_{T}$为张量传播速度。通过参数共振放大研究共振现象，当修正的摩擦项或传播速度以与背景标量场动力学匹配的频率振荡时。计算随机引力波背景（SBGW）谱增强：$\\Omega_{\\text{GW}}(f) = \\Omega_{\\text{GW}}^{\\text{prim}}(f) \\times \\mathcal{R}(f; \\theta_{\\text{model}}, r, n_{t})$，其中$\\mathcal{R}$是共振增强因子，依赖于模型参数$\\theta_{\\text{model}}$和原始张量谱参数（张量-标量比$r$，张量谱指数$n_{t}$）。

Result: The analysis demonstrates that resonant modifications in scalar-tensor theories can significantly amplify the stochastic gravitational wave background through parametric resonance effects. The enhancement factor $\\mathcal{R}(f)$ exhibits characteristic peaked features in the frequency domain, with peak positions and amplitudes sensitive to both the fundamental theory parameters (scalar field mass, coupling constants, oscillation frequencies) and primordial tensor spectrum parameters. These peaks can bring otherwise unobservable primordial tensor signals ($r < 10^{-10}$ in standard scenarios) into the detection sensitivity bands of LISA ($10^{-4}$ to $10^{-1}$ Hz) and Einstein Telescope ($1$ to $10^{3}$ Hz). The resonance mechanism effectively converts high-frequency scalar field oscillations into low-frequency GW spectral features via modulation of propagation characteristics, creating observable signatures even when the direct scalar field energy density is subdominant.

分析表明，标量-张量理论中的共振修正可以通过参数共振效应显著放大随机引力波背景。增强因子$\\mathcal{R}(f)$在频域中表现出特征性的峰值结构，峰值位置和振幅对基本理论参数（标量场质量、耦合常数、振荡频率）和原始张量谱参数都很敏感。这些峰值可以将原本不可观测的原始张量信号（标准情景下$r < 10^{-10}$）带入LISA（$10^{-4}$至$10^{-1}$ Hz）和爱因斯坦望远镜（$1$至$10^{3}$ Hz）的探测灵敏度带。共振机制通过传播特性的调制，有效地将高频标量场振荡转换为低频GW谱特征，即使标量场能量密度次主导时也能产生可观测特征。

Conclusion: Resonant enhancement of primordial gravitational waves in scalar-tensor extensions of gravity provides a novel and powerful mechanism to probe both fundamental gravity theories and early Universe physics. The characteristic peaked signatures in the stochastic GW spectrum serve as smoking gun evidence for such modifications, offering a pathway to constrain or detect otherwise inaccessible physics beyond the Standard Model and standard cosmology. This resonance amplification effectively bridges the gap between feeble primordial tensor signals and experimental sensitivity thresholds of next-generation detectors, potentially enabling direct observation of tensor modes from inflation, phase transitions, or other early Universe phenomena.

标量-张量引力扩展中原始引力波的共振增强提供了一种新颖而有力的机制来探测基本引力理论和早期宇宙物理学。随机GW谱中的特征峰值特征可作为此类修改的确凿证据，为限制或探测标准模型和标准宇宙学之外原本无法触及的物理学提供了途径。这种共振放大有效地弥合了微弱原始张量信号与下一代探测器实验灵敏度阈值之间的差距，可能实现对来自暴胀、相变或其他早期宇宙现象的张量模式的直接观测。

Abstract: Gravitational waves constitute a powerful probe of the underlying theory of gravity. In extensions of general relativity, additional degrees of freedom, such as scalar fields in the gravitational sector, can modify their propagation through changes in the effective friction term and propagation speed. These modifications may potentially induce resonant phenomena leading to distinctive signatures in the gravitational wave spectrum. One important aspect to be investigated is whether the resonances can be strong enough to enhance the underlying background of primordial tensor modes to levels detectable by upcoming gravitational wave detectors, such as LISA or the Einstein telescope. The characteristic peaks in the SBGW spectrum depend on the parameters of the resonant model as well as on the parameters of the primordial tensor spectrum, such as $r$ and $n_{t}$. Thus these resonance effects open a powerful pathway to explore physics of the very early Universe by amplifying otherwise feeble signals to experimentally detectable levels. Here we analyze how the signals of the primordial Universe can resonate in these scenarios, bringing the early universe physics into the realm of experimental access.

### [62] [The influence of plasma lensing magnification to the luminosity function of fast radio bursts](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.12691)
*Xinzhong Er,Weishan Zhu,Shude Mao,Dongzi Li*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: This paper investigates how plasma lensing by ionized gas clumps in the interstellar and circumgalactic media affects fast radio burst (FRB) luminosity functions, analyzing both demagnification (loss of faint sources) and magnification (creation of anomalously bright sources) using Gaussian plasma lens models across multiple planes.

该论文研究了星际和环星系介质中电离气体团块引起的等离子体透镜效应对快速射电暴（FRB）光度函数的影响，分析了使用高斯等离子体透镜模型在多个平面上的去放大效应（暗弱源损失）和放大效应（异常亮源的产生）。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Observations suggest the presence of small-scale ionized gas clumps in both the interstellar medium (ISM) and circumgalactic medium (CGM). These plasma inhomogeneities can deflect radio signals through plasma lensing, causing magnification and demagnification of background sources. This lensing effect distorts observed luminosity functions and may introduce systematic biases in population studies of radio sources like fast radio bursts (FRBs), potentially affecting cosmological inferences and source property measurements.

观测表明，在星际介质（ISM）和环星系介质（CGM）中都存在小尺度的电离气体团块。这些等离子体不均匀性可以通过等离子体透镜效应偏转射电信号，导致背景源的放大和去放大。这种透镜效应会扭曲观测到的光度函数，并可能对快速射电暴（FRB）等射电源的群体研究引入系统偏差，从而可能影响宇宙学推论和源属性测量。

Method: The study models plasma lensing effects on FRBs using Gaussian plasma clumps distributed across multiple lens planes within a small field of view. Key methodological components include: 1) Sampling central electron densities for each clump from uniform, log-normal, and Gaussian distributions to represent different ionized gas models; 2) Employing two analytical models to mimic the intrinsic luminosity function of FRBs; 3) Calculating lensing magnification effects and their impact on observed luminosity distributions; 4) Investigating the correlation between lensing strength and the power spectrum of free electron density; 5) Assessing how scattering effects in the host galaxy or Milky Way can suppress plasma lensing effects.

该研究使用分布在小视场内多个透镜平面上的高斯等离子体团块来模拟等离子体透镜效应对FRB的影响。关键方法包括：1）从均匀、对数正态和高斯分布中采样每个团块的中心电子密度，以表示不同的电离气体模型；2）采用两种解析模型来模拟FRB的本征光度函数；3）计算透镜放大效应及其对观测光度分布的影响；4）研究透镜强度与自由电子密度功率谱的相关性；5）评估宿主星系或银河系中的散射效应如何抑制等离子体透镜效应。

Result: The analysis reveals that plasma lensing significantly modifies observed FRB luminosity functions through two competing effects: 1) Demagnification can push sources below detection thresholds, with strength varying between approximately 1-15% depending on the ionized gas model and source redshift; 2) Magnification can produce anomalously bright sources at the high-luminosity end. Both effects introduce potential biases in inferred source properties. The lensing strength correlates with the power spectrum of free electron density, providing a potential observational signature. However, scattering effects in the host galaxy or Milky Way can suppress the plasma lensing effects, potentially mitigating some observational biases.

分析表明，等离子体透镜效应通过两种竞争效应显著改变了观测到的FRB光度函数：1）去放大效应可将源推至探测阈值以下，其强度根据电离气体模型和源红移在大约1-15%之间变化；2）放大效应可在高光度端产生异常亮的源。这两种效应都会在推断的源属性中引入潜在偏差。透镜强度与自由电子密度功率谱相关，这提供了一种潜在的观测特征。然而，宿主星系或银河系中的散射效应可以抑制等离子体透镜效应，可能减轻一些观测偏差。

Conclusion: Plasma lensing by ionized gas clumps in the ISM and CGM introduces systematic biases in FRB population studies by modifying luminosity functions through both demagnification and magnification effects. The strength of these effects depends on the specific ionized gas model and source redshift, and correlates with the power spectrum of free electron density. While scattering in host galaxies or the Milky Way can suppress lensing effects, careful consideration of plasma lensing is essential for accurate cosmological inferences and source property measurements from FRB observations. The work highlights the importance of accounting for small-scale plasma inhomogeneities in precision radio astronomy.

ISM和CGM中电离气体团块引起的等离子体透镜效应通过去放大和放大效应改变光度函数，从而在FRB群体研究中引入系统偏差。这些效应的强度取决于具体的电离气体模型和源红移，并与自由电子密度功率谱相关。虽然宿主星系或银河系中的散射可以抑制透镜效应，但为了从FRB观测中获得准确的宇宙学推论和源属性测量，必须仔细考虑等离子体透镜效应。这项工作强调了在精密射电天文学中考虑小尺度等离子体不均匀性的重要性。

Abstract: Small scale clumps of ionized gas have been suggested by observations in interstellar medium and circumgalactic medium. The propagation of radio signals can be deflected by these plasma clumps, i.e. plasma lensing. One observable consequence is the magnification and demagnification of background sources. These effects distort the observed luminosity function and potentially introduce bias into population studies. In this work, we investigate these effects on fast radio bursts using Gaussian plasma clumps distributed across multiple lens planes within a small field of view. The central electron density for each clump is sampled from uniform, log-normal, and Gaussian distributions. Two analytical models are employed to mimic the intrinsic luminosity function. Our results show that plasma lensing can modify the observed luminosity functions. On one hand, our model shows that radio sources may be demagnified below the detection threshold, the strength varies between ~1-15% depending on the ionized gas model and the source redshift. On the other hand, magnification can produce anomalously bright sources at the high luminosity end. Both effects introduce potential biases in inferred source properties. The lensing strength correlates with the power spectrum of free electron density. However, scattering effect in the host galaxy or in the Milky Way can suppress the plasma lensing effects.

### [63] [Halo abundance and clustering in cosmologies with massive and asymmetric neutrinos](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.12801)
*Yizhou Liu,Wangzheng Zhang,Shihong Liao,Liang Gao*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: This study examines how neutrino mass and asymmetry parameter affect halo mass function and bias using N-body simulations. Neutrino mass suppresses massive halo formation, while asymmetry enhances it, with effects amplifying at higher redshifts.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Neutrinos are abundant fermions influencing large-scale structure formation through both their non-zero masses and potential chemical asymmetry. While neutrino mass effects have been studied extensively, the role of neutrino asymmetry (characterized by parameter $η^{2}$) remains poorly explored, motivating investigation into how both neutrino properties modify halo formation and clustering.

Method: The authors employ cosmological N-body simulations with refitted cosmological parameters consistent with CMB observations. They systematically vary neutrino mass ($M_ν=0-0.24\,\mathrm{eV}$) and asymmetry parameter ($η^{2}=0-0.8$) to analyze modifications to halo mass function (HMF) and halo bias. Simulations track evolution across redshifts including z=0, 2, 4, and 9, comparing results to massless neutrino case.

Result: Neutrino mass suppresses massive halo abundance (up to ~30% reduction at z=0 for $M_ν=0.24\,\mathrm{eV}$), while neutrino asymmetry enhances HMF across broad mass range (up to ~5% at z=0 for $η^{2}=0.8$). Effects intensify at higher redshifts: at z=4 and z=9, asymmetry enhances HMF by ~25% and ~75% respectively, while mass suppression deepens to ~40% and ~70%. For halo bias, neutrino mass enhances bias for halos above $10^{13.4}\,\mathrm{M_\odot}$ (up to ~5% at z=0), while asymmetry reduces bias by few percent on linear scales. These trends strengthen with redshift, reaching ~15% enhancement and ~10% suppression at z=2. Linear bias models provide adequate but not exact description.

Conclusion: Halo abundance and clustering serve as sensitive probes for both neutrino mass and asymmetry. Neutrino mass suppresses massive halo formation while enhancing large-scale bias, whereas neutrino asymmetry enhances halo abundance while reducing bias. These opposing effects become increasingly pronounced at higher redshifts, offering potential discriminants in cosmological observations. The findings demonstrate significant cosmological signatures beyond standard neutrino mass effects.

Abstract: Neutrinos are the most abundant fermions in the Universe and influence the formation of large-scale structure through both their non-zero masses and a possible chemical potential which can be described by a single asymmetry parameter. While most previous studies have focused on the impact of the neutrino mass, the role of neutrino asymmetry remains comparatively unexplored. In this work, we investigate how massive neutrinos ($M_ν=0-0.24\,\mathrm{eV}$) with a non-zero asymmetry parameter ($η^{2}=0-0.8$) modify the halo mass function (HMF) and halo bias using cosmological N-body simulations with cosmological parameters consistently refitted to CMB observations. We find that at all redshifts, neutrino mass suppresses the abundance of massive halos, whereas neutrino asymmetry enhances the HMF over a broad mass range. At z=0, the abundance of the most massive halos is reduced by up to ~30% in the largest-mass case ($M_ν=0.24\,\mathrm{eV}$), while neutrino asymmetry ($η^{2}=0.8$) produces a maximum ~5% enhancement. These effects become increasingly pronounced at higher redshifts: by z=4 and z=9, the enhancement induced by neutrino asymmetry reaches ~25% and ~75%, respectively, while the corresponding suppression due to neutrino mass deepens to below ~40% and ~70% of the massless case. For halo bias, we find that halos with masses above $10^{13.4}\,\mathrm{M_\odot}$ exhibit an enhanced large-scale bias due to neutrino mass, reaching up to ~5% at z=0, while neutrino asymmetry reduces the bias by a few percent on linear scales. These trends strengthen with redshift, with the enhancement and suppression growing to ~15% and ~10% at z=2, respectively. Linear bias models provide an adequate, though not exact, description of halo bias in massive-neutrino cosmologies. Our results demonstrate that halo abundance and clustering offer sensitive probes of both neutrino mass and asymmetry.

</details>


### [64] [Simulation-based inference from the Lyman-alpha forest 1D power spectrum with CAMELS](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13011)
*Francesco Sinigaglia,Patricia Iglesias-Navarro,Matteo Viel*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: First full simulation-based inference on Lyman-α forest 1D power spectrum using CAMELS simulations with IllustrisTNG and SIMBA models. Neural posterior estimation of cosmological ($\Omega_m$, $\sigma_8$) and astrophysical parameters shows excellent accuracy (within 10% for ~75-90% of cases) when training/testing on same model, but suffers from ~10% bias when training/testing across models. Multi-domain training combining both models eliminates bias.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Traditional Lyman-α forest analyses face challenges from systematic uncertainties in baryonic physics and galaxy formation models. Simulation-based inference offers a rigorous approach to propagate these uncertainties, but cross-model generalization remains problematic due to lack of convergence between different hydrodynamical simulations.

Method: Uses CAMELS cosmological hydrodynamic simulations with IllustrisTNG and SIMBA galaxy formation models. Trains normalizing flow for neural posterior estimation of two cosmological parameters ($\Omega_m$, $\sigma_8$) and four astrophysical parameters (supernova and AGN feedback). Employs multi-domain training strategy combining simulations from both models to address cross-model bias.

Result: Within-model inference achieves excellent accuracy: $\Omega_m$ within 10% for $\gtrsim 75\%$ cases, $\sigma_8$ within 10% for $\gtrsim 90\%$ cases, both with better than 10% precision. Astrophysical parameters generally unconstrained due to limited volume. Cross-model inference shows ~10% positive bias on $\sigma_8$. Multi-domain training recovers unbiased constraints, resolving the cross-model bias problem.

Conclusion: Demonstrates feasibility of simulation-based inference for Lyman-α forest cosmology with AI. Multi-domain training provides robust solution to model discrepancy issues, enabling extraction of unbiased cosmological parameters from next-generation surveys despite uncertain baryonic physics.

Abstract: We perform for the first time full simulation-based inference on the Lyman-$α$ forest 1D power spectrum. In particular, we consider the prediction of the Lyman-$α$ forest $P_{\rm 1D}(k)$ at $2.0<z<3.5$ from the CAMELS cosmological hydrodynamic simulations run with the IllustrisTNG and SIMBA galaxy formation models. We train a normalizing flow to perform neural posterior estimation of two cosmological parameters ($Ω_m$ and $σ_8$) and four astrophysical parameters parametrizing supernova and AGN feedback. When training and testing the neural network on the same baryon physics model, the posterior distributions of the cosmological parameters are found to be in excellent agreement with the true parameters values (within $10\%$ deviations in $\gtrsim 75\%$ and $\gtrsim 90\%$ of the cases for $Ω_m$ and $σ_8$, and a precision better than $10\%$ in both), while the astrophysical parameters are generally unconstrained due to the limited probed volume. When training on one model and testing on the other (e.g., training on IllustrisTNG and testing on SIMBA, or viceversa), the performance is significantly worse, both in accuracy and in precision, resulting in a $\sim 10\%$ positive bias on the predicted values for $σ_8$. We show that a multi-domain training based on the combination of simulations from both models recovers unbiased constraints, offering an effective solution to cope with the complex problem of the lack of convergence in the predictions from different galaxy formation models. This study represents a promising way forward to constrain cosmology and fundamental physics with the Lyman-$α$ forest with artificial intelligence.

*Evan Saraivanov,Henrique Rubira,Vivian Miranda,Tim Eifler*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: A comprehensive forecast framework for Roman Space Telescope cosmic shear using two-loop Effective Field Theory of Large-Scale Structure (EFTofLSS) with neural network emulators, redshift-dependent counterterm calibration against hydrodynamical simulations, and principal component analysis to handle baryonic feedback systematics.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Stage IV weak lensing surveys require non-linear modeling of the matter power spectrum that maintains accuracy across scales and redshifts while being robust to baryonic feedback effects. The two-loop EFTofLSS offers a controlled expansion framework, but its application to continuous redshift cosmic shear data introduces substantial parameter complexity requiring systematic mitigation.

Method: Develop neural network emulators for rapid evaluation of two-loop EFT integrals. Calibrate redshift-dependent counterterms against Euclid Emulator 2, parameterizing residual redshift freedom with spline functions. Perform principal component analysis to reduce dimensionality, then calibrate priors using hydrodynamical simulation suites. Forecast $S_8$ constraints for Roman Space Telescope with scale cut optimization.

Result: Two-loop EFT achieves unbiased $S_8=σ_8\sqrt{Ω_{\rm m}/0.3}$ constraints with relative errors of ~0.9% (5% UV mode contamination) and ~1.4% (1% contamination), outperforming one-loop EFT and non-linear dark matter-only models when baryonic effects are included. The framework extends scale reach while maintaining theoretical control.

Conclusion: The two-loop EFTofLSS framework with neural network emulation and principled parameter reduction provides a robust pathway for extracting cosmological information from small-scale cosmic shear data in Stage IV surveys, balancing theoretical precision with practical parameter estimation in the presence of baryonic feedback.

Abstract: Extracting cosmological information from Stage IV weak lensing surveys requires non-linear modelling of the matter power spectrum that is accurate across a broad range of scales and redshifts and robust to baryonic feedback. We forecast the application of the two-loop effective field theory of large-scale structure (EFTofLSS) to Roman Space Telescope, carefully considering parameterization, scale cuts, and priors. We develop neural network emulators for the two-loop integrals, allowing rapid evaluation of the likelihood. Weak lensing demands a continuous-in-redshift description of the EFT, potentially introducing tens of nuisance parameters. We address this by calibrating the counterterm redshift evolution against the Euclid Emulator 2 and accounting for the residual freedom in redshift with spline functions. A principal component analysis of the free parameters reduces the dimensionality to a few degrees of freedom that the data can constrain. Next, we calibrate the priors on those degrees of freedom by using a suite of hydrodynamical simulations. We forecast the $S_8$ constraints as a function of scale cuts, showing that the two-loop EFT with Roman cosmic shear provides unbiased $S_8=σ_8\sqrt{Ω_{\rm m}/0.3}$ constraints with relative errors of about $0.9\%$ and $1.4\%$ when allowing for $5\%$ and $1\%$ contamination from ultraviolet modes, respectively. The two-loop EFT improves the scale reach beyond the one-loop EFT and non-linear dark matter-only models when baryonic effects are included. This framework provides a robust path for extracting small-scale information from future cosmic shear data.

### [66] [A unified harmonic framework for dark siren cosmology](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13053)
*April Qiu Cheng,Jonathan Gair*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: The paper presents the galaxy catalog dark siren cross-correlation method as an extension of standard dark siren techniques, enabling cosmological inference from gravitational waves without electromagnetic counterparts by statistically marginalizing over unknown host galaxies through 2-point statistics and incorporating measurement errors. Combined with spectral sirens and next-generation detectors, this approach promises precise joint constraints on cosmological parameters like $H_0$ and $\Omega_{m,0}$.

本文提出星系目录暗警报交叉相关方法作为标准暗警报技术的扩展，通过利用两点统计在未知宿主星系的统计边际化基础上，实现无需电磁对应体的引力波宇宙学推断，并纳入测量误差。结合光谱警报和下一代探测器，该方法有望对宇宙学参数如$H_0$和$\Omega_{m,0}$提供精确联合约束。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Standard dark siren methods relying on galaxy catalogs face challenges in host identification and scale poorly with increasing GW catalog sizes in next-generation experiments. The cross-correlation approach offers a statistically rigorous framework that bypasses individual host assignments, leveraging ensemble information through correlation functions while systematically incorporating GW measurement uncertainties.

标准依赖星系目录的暗警报方法在宿主识别上面临挑战，并且随着下一代实验中引力波目录规模的增加，其可扩展性较差。交叉相关方法提供了一个统计上严格的框架，通过相关函数绕过个体宿主分配，利用整体信息，同时系统地纳入引力波测量不确定性。

Method: The method extends the galaxy catalog dark siren formalism by replacing explicit host marginalization with statistical averaging over all possible galaxy field realizations using correlation functions. It combines: (1) GW-galaxy angular cross-correlation incorporating clustering information; (2) spectral sirens for rate evolution and mass distribution; (3) rigorous likelihood construction including GW measurement errors; and (4) joint inference framework integrating all dark siren constraints. The formalism connects to standard methods via the Limber approximation and requires assumptions about galaxy bias and GW selection effects.

该方法通过使用相关函数替换显式宿主边际化，采用对所有可能星系场实现的统计平均，扩展了星系目录暗警报形式体系。它结合了：(1)包含聚类信息的引力波-星系角向交叉相关；(2)速率演化和质量分布的光谱警报；(3)包含引力波测量误差的严格似然函数构造；(4)整合所有暗警报约束的联合推断框架。该形式体系通过Limber近似与标准方法相联系，并需要关于星系偏置和引力波选择效应的假设。

Result: Analysis shows the cross-correlation component alone, with a 2 Einstein Telescope + 1 Cosmic Explorer configuration over 2 years, can achieve 1\% precision on $H_0$ and 5\% on $\Omega_{m,0}$ through joint constraints. The method demonstrates superior scaling properties compared to canonical population inference techniques that struggle with large catalogs. However, current-generation detectors likely lack sufficient statistics for robust cross-correlation inference, requiring next-generation instruments for practical implementation.

分析表明，仅交叉相关部分在使用2个爱因斯坦望远镜+1个宇宙探索者配置运行2年的情况下，可以通过联合约束实现对$H_0$的1\%精度和$\Omega_{m,0}$的5\%精度。与处理大型目录时存在困难的典型总体推断技术相比，该方法展现出更优越的扩展性。然而，当前一代探测器可能缺乏足够的统计数据用于可靠的交叉相关推断，需要下一代仪器才能实际实施。

Conclusion: The GW-galaxy cross-correlation method represents a theoretically robust extension to dark siren cosmology that transforms the challenge of unknown host galaxies into a statistical advantage through ensemble correlations. When combined with spectral sirens and next-generation GW detectors, it offers a scalable pathway to precision cosmology without electromagnetic counterparts. The approach fundamentally changes the inference paradigm from individual source identification to population-level statistics, making it well-suited for the data-rich era of third-generation GW observatories.

引力波-星系交叉相关方法代表了对暗警报宇宙学在理论上的稳健扩展，通过整体相关性将未知宿主星系的挑战转化为统计优势。与光谱警报和下一代引力波探测器结合时，它为无需电磁对应体的精确宇宙学提供了一条可扩展的途径。该方法从根本上改变了推断范式，从个体源识别转向总体水平统计，使其特别适合第三代引力波天文台的数据丰富时代。

Abstract: The galaxy catalog dark siren method aims to infer cosmological parameters from gravitational waves (GWs) without an electromagnetic counterpart by statistically marginalizing over possible host galaxies. The cross-correlation of GW sources and galaxies is a promising avenue for cosmological inference without requiring observed host galaxies, by leveraging 2-point statistics. We provide a detailed guide to the cross-correlation method, clarifying its relationship to standard dark siren techniques as well as the assumptions necessary to be able to use this formalism on GW data. We show that the cross-correlation method is an extension of the angular part of the galaxy catalog method in which we effectively marginalize over all possible realizations of the unknown galaxy field, jointly adding information from galaxy--galaxy clustering. Combined with the spectral sirens method, which encodes information from the GW rate evolution, mass distribution, and selection effects, one can perform an inference that leverages the joint constraining power of all dark siren methods. We also present a strategy to rigorously fold GW measurement errors into the likelihood. Using this method, we show that with a 2 Einstein Telescope + 1 Cosmic Explorer setup, the GW--galaxy cross-correlation part alone can jointly measure $H_0$ and $Ω_{m,0}$ to 1\% and 5\% precision with just 2 years of data, demonstrating its potential as a precise and scalable inference technique in the next generation of GW and galaxy surveys. This is in contrast with canonical population inference techniques, which are known to scale poorly with the precision and catalog size expected of next-generation GW experiments. Contrary to some previous projections, we remain pessimistic about the cross-correlation method until these next generation detectors are online, due to its implicit requirement of large-number statistics.

Abstract: Gravitational-wave (GW) dark sirens provide an independent probe of the cosmic expansion history. Multiband GW observations can track GW events across different frequency bands and thus improve both. Motivated by this, we forecast the cosmological potential of intermediate-mass black hole binaries (IMBHBs) observed by a three-band GW detector network composed of Taiji (TJ), the Lunar Gravitational-wave Antenna (LGWA), and the Einstein Telescope (ET). <details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To establish a first-principles physical understanding of how baryons are expelled from dark matter haloes, quantifying the interplay between gravitational collapse, hydrostatic pressure, cosmic expansion, and especially the role of dark energy in baryon evacuation.

Method: An analytical model based on equilibrium between gravitational attraction, hydrostatic pressure support, and cosmological expansion effects (Hubble flow). Derives closure radius $R_{\rm cl}$ from mass conservation: $M_b(<R_{\rm cl})/M_{\rm tot}(<R_{\rm cl}) = f_b = Ω_b/Ω_m$. Compares with six EAGLE simulation variants spanning $Λ/Λ_0 = 0$ to $100$.

Result: Excellent agreement ($<10\%$ deviation) between analytical predictions and simulations for haloes $M_{\rm 200c} > 10^{11} M_\odot$ at $0<z<3$. Dark energy significantly enhances baryon evacuation: $R_{\rm cl}(Λ_0) ∼ 30\%$ larger than Einstein-de Sitter at $z<2$. For $Λ ≥ 10Λ_0$, dark energy dominates evacuation.

Abstract: The extent to which galactic-scale astrophysical processes conspire with the underlying cosmological model to expel baryons from haloes remains a central question in galaxy formation. We present an analytical model for the gas distribution within and beyond haloes, based on the balance between gravitational collapse, hydrostatic pressure, and cosmic expansion. Our model predicts, from first principles, the halo-centric distance enclosing a baryon mass fraction equal to the cosmic value $f_{\rm b} = Ω_{\rm b}/Ω_{\rm m}$ (`closure radius') in an arbitrary $Λ$CDM cosmology. We compare the predictions with the results of six variants of the EAGLE cosmological, hydrodynamical simulation, encompassing values of the cosmological constant ranging from 0 to 100 times its observed value in our Universe, $Λ_0$. Despite its simplicity, our model exhibits excellent agreement with the simulations for haloes with mass $M_{\rm 200c} > 10^{11} M_\odot$ in the redshift range $0<z<3$, suggesting that it captures the key astrophysical processes and highlighting its robustness to the cosmological parameters. Thus, it provides the first physical explanation for the empirical closure radius-halo mass relation previously observed in simulations. Furthermore, we find that dark energy plays a non-negligible role in baryon evacuation: the simulations reveal that in the fiducial cosmological model, the closure radius at $z<2$ is $\sim 30\%$ larger than in an Einstein-de Sitter universe. In cosmologies with $Λ\geq 10 Λ_0$, dark energy emerges as the dominant factor in this process -- suggesting that, as our Universe transitions towards $Λ$-domination, dark energy eventually becomes the primary driver of baryon evacuation from massive haloes.

### [69] [Ridged Lagrangian Perturbation Theory (RLPT)](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13106)
*Francisco-Shu Kitaura,Francesco Sinigaglia*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: We propose Ridged Lagrangian Perturbation Theory (RLPT), a two-step forward model that combines standard long-range LPT transport with an explicit Eulerian ridging step. This post-processing update reconstructs short-range, curl-free displacements from the realized density field through scale separation and Poisson inversion, improving nonlinear power and field-level agreement while preserving large-scale phases.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current single-step Lagrangian Perturbation Theory (LPT) solvers for large-scale structure forward models are efficient but suffer from overly diffuse filaments and knots, underpredicting small-scale clustering. Galaxy surveys require fast models that preserve large-scale phases while providing realistic nonlinear morphology at fixed force resolution.

Method: RLPT is a modular two-step scheme: (1) Standard long-range LPT/ALPT transport, followed by (2) an explicit Eulerian ridging update. This post-processing step reconstructs a short-range, curl-free displacement from the realized density field through smooth scale separation and Poisson inversion. The ridging layer is inexpensive, preserves the large-scale solution, and offers transparent parameters to tune the short-range response.

Result: RLPT systematically improves both nonlinear power spectrum and field-level agreement relative to 2LPT/ALPT baselines when tested against particle-mesh and $N$-body references. Additionally, ridging can function as a deterministic subgrid relocation model, enabling controlled tuning of tracer clustering beyond nominal resolution, which is valuable for mock-galaxy production and observational systematics sensitive to close pairs.

Conclusion: Ridged Lagrangian Perturbation Theory provides an effective framework for improving LPT-based forward models by explicitly adding short-scale ridging corrections. The method offers substantial improvements in small-scale clustering while maintaining computational efficiency and large-scale accuracy, making it particularly suitable for mock catalog generation and systematics-sensitive analyses in galaxy surveys.

Abstract: Galaxy surveys demand fast large-scale structure forward models that preserve large-scale phases while providing realistic nonlinear morphology at fixed force resolution. Single-step Lagrangian Perturbation Theory (LPT) solvers are efficient, but they typically yield overly diffuse filaments and knots and underpredict small-scale clustering.
  We introduce Ridged Lagrangian Perturbation Theory (RLPT), a modular two-step scheme: a standard long-range LPT/ALPT transport is followed by a single post-processing Eulerian {ridging} update that reconstructs a short-range, curl-free displacement from the realised density field through a smooth scale separation and a Poisson inversion. This explicit completion layer is inexpensive, preserves the large-scale solution, and provides a small set of transparent parameters to tune the short-range response.
  We test RLPT against particle-mesh and $N$-body references and find that one additional ridging step systematically improves both nonlinear power and field-level agreement relative to 2LPT/ALPT baselines. Finally, we demonstrate that ridging can be repurposed as a deterministic subgrid relocation model: even when the underlying dark-matter field is only ``good enough'' on the mesh, ridging enables controlled tuning of tracer clustering beyond the nominal resolution, which is particularly relevant for mock-galaxy production and observational systematics sensitive to close pairs.

宇宙学常数问题和哈勃张力对标准ΛCDM范式构成挑战，促使探索动态暗能量替代方案。临界涌现暗能量（CEDE）提供了一种特定机制：暗能量仅通过相变在临界时期后涌现，可能解决观测张力同时保持早期宇宙的简单性。

Method: Comprehensive Bayesian parameter inference using Markov Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) methods applied to CEDE cosmological framework. Observational constraints derived from: Planck 2018 CMB data; SDSS and DESI DR2 BAO measurements; two independent Type Ia supernova compilations (PantheonPlus and Union3). Statistical assessment via Δχ² comparisons and Bayesian evidence ratios against ΛCDM baseline. Phase transition characterized by critical scale factor $a_c$ where dark energy density undergoes dynamical emergence.

\n\n
采用马尔可夫链蒙特卡洛（MCMC）方法对CEDE宇宙学框架进行全面的贝叶斯参数推断。观测约束来自：Planck 2018 CMB数据；SDSS和DESI DR2的BAO测量；两个独立的Ia型超新星汇编（PantheonPlus和Union3）。通过Δχ²比较和相对于ΛCDM基线的贝叶斯证据比进行统计评估。相变通过临界尺度因子$a_c$表征，此时暗能量密度发生动态涌现。

Result: Phase transition in CEDE not ruled out by current data; CMB-only, CMB+SDSS, and CMB+DESI datasets provide evidence for nonzero transition scale factor $a_c > 0$. According to Δχ² and Bayesian evidence criteria, CEDE can be favored over ΛCDM for these specific data combinations. However, CEDE does not fully resolve the Hubble constant tension ($H_0$ discrepancy). Model viability maintained across observational probes without strong inconsistencies.

\n\n
当前数据不排除CEDE中的相变；仅CMB、CMB+SDSS和CMB+DESI数据集提供了非零相变尺度因子$a_c > 0$的证据。根据Δχ²和贝叶斯证据标准，对于这些特定数据组合，CEDE可能优于ΛCDM。然而，CEDE未完全解决哈勃常数张力（$H_0$ discrepancy）。模型在所有观测探针中保持可行性，无强烈不一致性。

Conclusion: CEDE represents phenomenologically viable extension to ΛCDM with phase transition mechanism that remains compatible with current cosmological observations. Model demonstrates capability to improve fit to certain data combinations, suggesting dynamical dark energy emergence through critical epoch warrants further investigation. Future high-precision surveys (DESI, Euclid, Roman) essential to distinguish between genuine departure from ΛCDM versus effective description of current data limitations.

\n\n
CEDE代表了ΛCDM的现象学可行扩展，其相变机制与当前宇宙学观测保持兼容。模型展示了对特定数据组合改善拟合的能力，表明通过临界时期的动态暗能量涌现值得进一步研究。未来的高精度巡天（DESI、Euclid、Roman）对于区分是真正偏离ΛCDM还是对当前数据局限的有效描述至关重要。

Abstract: We investigate a specific emergent dark energy scenario, known as critically emergent dark energy (CEDE), in which dark energy is effectively absent in the early Universe and becomes dynamically relevant only after a critical cosmic epoch through a phase transition. We constrain this model using recent cosmological observations, including cosmic microwave background (CMB) data from \emph{Planck} 2018, baryon acoustic oscillation (BAO) measurements from SDSS and DESI DR2, and two independent Type Ia supernova compilations, PantheonPlus and Union3. Our results show that within the CEDE framework a dark energy phase transition is not ruled out. In particular, CMB-only, CMB+SDSS, and CMB+DESI datasets provide evidence for a nonzero transition scale factor and, according to standard statistical indicators such as $Δχ^2$ and Bayesian evidence, can favor CEDE over the $Λ$CDM model. At the same time, we find that CEDE does not fully resolve the Hubble constant tension. Overall, our analysis indicates that dark energy models featuring a phase transition remain a viable and phenomenologically interesting extension of the standard cosmological framework. Upcoming high-precision cosmological surveys will be essential to further assess whether such emergent dark energy scenarios represent a genuine departure from $Λ$CDM or an effective description of current data.

</details>


### [71] [Euclid preparation. Simulated galaxy catalogues for non-standard cosmological models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13148)
*Euclid Collaboration,M. -A. Breton,P. Fosalba,S. Avila,M. Baldi,C. Carbone,M. Kärcher,G. Rácz,M. Bolzonella,F. J. Castander,C. Giocoli,K. Koyama,A. M. C. Le Brun,L. Pozzetti,A. G. Adame,V. Gonzalez-Perez,G. Yepes,B. Altieri,S. Andreon,C. Baccigalupi,S. Bardelli,P. Battaglia,A. Biviano,E. Branchini,M. Brescia,S. Camera,V. Capobianco,V. F. Cardone,J. Carretero,M. Castellano,G. Castignani,S. Cavuoti,A. Cimatti,C. Colodro-Conde,G. Congedo,L. Conversi,Y. Copin,A. Costille,F. Courbin,H. M. Courtois,A. Da Silva,H. Degaudenzi,S. de la Torre,G. De Lucia,H. Dole,M. Douspis,F. Dubath,C. A. J. Duncan,X. Dupac,S. Dusini,S. Escoffier,M. Farina,R. Farinelli,S. Farrens,F. Faustini,S. Ferriol,F. Finelli,S. Fotopoulou,N. Fourmanoit,M. Frailis,E. Franceschi,M. Fumana,S. Galeotta,K. George,B. Gillis,J. Gracia-Carpio,A. Grazian,F. Grupp,S. V. H. Haugan,W. Holmes,F. Hormuth,A. Hornstrup,K. Jahnke,M. Jhabvala,B. Joachimi,S. Kermiche,A. Kiessling,M. Kilbinger,B. Kubik,M. Kunz,H. Kurki-Suonio,S. Ligori,P. B. Lilje,V. Lindholm,I. Lloro,G. Mainetti,O. Mansutti,O. Marggraf,M. Martinelli,N. Martinet,F. Marulli,R. J. Massey,E. Medinaceli,S. Mei,M. Meneghetti,E. Merlin,G. Meylan,A. Mora,M. Moresco,L. Moscardini,C. Neissner,S. -M. Niemi,J. W. Nightingale,C. Padilla,S. Paltani,F. Pasian,K. Pedersen,V. Pettorino,S. Pires,G. Polenta,M. Poncet,L. A. Popa,F. Raison,A. Renzi,J. Rhodes,G. Riccio,E. Romelli,M. Roncarelli,R. Saglia,Z. Sakr,D. Sapone,B. Sartoris,A. Secroun,G. Seidel,E. Sihvola,P. Simon,C. Sirignano,G. Sirri,A. Spurio Mancini,L. Stanco,P. Tallada-Crespí,A. N. Taylor,I. Tereno,N. Tessore,S. Toft,R. Toledo-Moreo,F. Torradeflot,I. Tutusaus,E. A. Valentijn,J. Valiviita,T. Vassallo,G. Verdoes Kleijn,Y. Wang,J. Weller,G. Zamorani,F. M. Zerbi,E. Zucca,M. Ballardini,A. Boucaud,E. Bozzo,C. Burigana,R. Cabanac,M. Calabrese,A. Cappi,T. Castro,J. A. Escartin Vigo,G. Fabbian,L. Gabarra,J. García-Bellido,S. Hemmati,J. Macias-Perez,R. Maoli,J. Martín-Fleitas,N. Mauri,R. B. Metcalf,P. Monaco,A. Pezzotta,M. Pöntinen,I. Risso,V. Scottez,M. Sereno,M. Tenti,M. Tucci,M. Viel,M. Wiesmann,Y. Akrami,I. T. Andika,G. Angora,M. Archidiacono,F. Atrio-Barandela,L. Bazzanini,J. Bel,D. Bertacca,M. Bethermin,F. Beutler,A. Blanchard,L. Blot,M. Bonici,S. Borgani,M. L. Brown,S. Bruton,B. Camacho Quevedo,F. Caro,C. S. Carvalho,F. Gavazzi,E. Gaztanaga,F. Giacomini,F. Gianotti,G. Gozaliasl,A. Gruppuso,M. Guidi,C. M. Gutierrez,A. Hall,H. Hildebrandt,J. Hjorth,J. J. E. Kajava,Y. Kang,V. Kansal,D. Karagiannis,K. Kiiveri,J. Kim,C. C. Kirkpatrick,S. Kruk,M. Lattanzi,J. Le Graet,L. Legrand,M. Lembo,F. Lepori,G. Leroy,G. F. Lesci,J. Lesgourgues,T. I. Liaudat,S. J. Liu,X. Lopez Lopez,M. Magliocchetti,A. Manjón-García,F. Mannucci,C. J. A. P. Martins,L. Maurin,M. Miluzio,A. Montoro,C. Moretti,G. Morgante,S. Nadathur,K. Naidoo,A. Navarro-Alsina,S. Nesseris,L. Pagano,D. Paoletti,F. Passalacqua,K. Paterson,L. Patrizii,C. Pattison,A. Pisani,D. Potter,G. W. Pratt,S. Quai,M. Radovich,K. Rojas,W. Roster,S. Sacquegna,M. Sahlén,D. B. Sanders,E. Sarpa,A. Schneider,M. Schultheis,D. Sciotti,E. Sellentin,L. C. Smith,J. G. Sorce,K. Tanidis,F. Tarsitano,G. Testera,R. Teyssier,S. Tosi,A. Troja,C. Valieri,A. Venhola,D. Vergani,F. Vernizzi,G. Verza,S. Vinciguerra,N. A. Walton,A. H. Wright,H. W. Yeung*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: Stage-IV galaxy surveys like Euclid will test cosmological models with unprecedented precision. This work produces public simulated galaxy catalogues for non-standard cosmologies (modified gravity, alternative dark energy, massive neutrinos, primordial non-Gaussianity) using analytical pipelines. Analysis of galaxy clustering via redshift-space 2PCF multipoles and VDG model reveals that the parameter $f\sigma_{12}$ (linear growth rate times matter fluctuation amplitude) shows remarkable robustness across diverse cosmological templates, though template mismatch introduces additional scatter and can cause deviations larger than statistical errors.

下一代宇宙学巡天（如Euclid）将以前所未有的精度检验宇宙学模型。本研究为多种非标准宇宙学模型（修正引力、替代暗能量、大质量中微子、原初非高斯性）生成了公开的模拟星系巡天目录，并采用分析流程进行处理。通过红移空间两点相关函数多极矩和VDG模型对星系成团性的分析表明，参数$f\sigma_{12}$（线性增长率与物质涨落振幅的乘积）在不同宇宙学模板间表现出显著的稳健性，尽管模板不匹配会引入额外的弥散，并可能导致偏离超过统计误差。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Stage-IV galaxy surveys (Euclid, DESI, LSST, Roman) will deliver data of exceptional quality, enabling stringent tests of the cosmological concordance model (ΛCDM) and probing extensions like modified gravity, dynamical dark energy, massive neutrinos, and primordial non-Gaussianity. However, robust cosmological inference from these surveys requires accurate modeling of galaxy clustering, which depends on both cosmological background and the galaxy-halo connection. Previous analyses often assumed a specific cosmological template (e.g., ΛCDM) when interpreting data from simulations of non-standard models, potentially introducing biases. This study aims to systematically assess the impact of template choice on cosmological parameter inference, particularly focusing on the robustness of the combined parameter $f\sigma_{12}$, across a broad suite of non-standard cosmological simulations.

第四代星系巡天（如Euclid、DESI、LSST、Roman）将提供极其优质的数据，从而能够对宇宙学标准模型（ΛCDM）进行严格检验，并探测其扩展，如修正引力、动力学暗能量、大质量中微子以及原初非高斯性。然而，从这些巡天中获得稳健的宇宙学推断需要精确的星系成团性建模，这依赖于宇宙学背景和星系-晕关联。以往的分析在解释非标准模型的模拟数据时，通常假设特定的宇宙学模板（如ΛCDM），这可能会引入偏差。本研究旨在系统性地评估模板选择对宇宙学参数推断的影响，特别关注组合参数$f\sigma_{12}$在一系列广泛的非标准宇宙学模拟中的稳健性。

Method: 1. **Simulation Suite**: Produced simulated galaxy catalogues from a broad suite of cosmological N-body simulations encompassing non-standard models: Modified Gravity (e.g., $f(R)$, DGP), Alternative Dark Energy (e.g., quintessence, phantom), Massive Neutrinos (varying $\Sigma m_\nu$), and Primordial Non-Gaussianity (local $f_{NL}$).

2. **Halo Identification**: Used Rockstar halo finder to identify dark matter halos and subhalos from the simulation snapshots.

3. **Galaxy-Halo Connection**: Employed a modified version of the SciPic library to populate halos with galaxies using the Halo Occupation Distribution (HOD) framework. This provides a model-independent mapping between halo properties and galaxy statistics.

4. **Analytical Pipeline**: Processed simulations through a model-independent analytical pipeline to compute clustering statistics.

5. **Clustering Analysis**: Investigated galaxy-clustering characteristics via:
   - Multipoles of the two-point correlation function (2PCF) in redshift space: $\xi_\ell(s)$ for $\ell = 0,2,4,...$
   - VDG (Velocileptors-based Dark matter and Galaxy clustering): A highly performant effective field theory (EFT) model for galaxy clustering in redshift space, which parametrizes bias and redshift-space distortions.

6. **Parameter Inference**: Extracted cosmological parameters, with particular focus on the combined parameter $f\sigma_{12}$, where $f = d\ln D/d\ln a$ is the linear growth rate and $\sigma_{12}$ is the matter density fluctuation amplitude within spheres of radius $12\ \mathrm{Mpc}/h$.

7. **Template Testing**: Performed cosmological parameter inference using various cosmological models as "templates" when analyzing data from different underlying simulations, assessing the robustness and potential biases.

模拟方法：1. **模拟套件**：基于一系列广泛的非标准宇宙学模型的N体模拟，生成了模拟星系巡天目录，这些模型包括：修正引力（如$f(R)$、DGP）、替代暗能量（如quintessence、phantom）、大质量中微子（变化$\Sigma m_\nu$）以及原初非高斯性（local $f_{NL}$）。

2. **晕识别**：使用Rockstar晕查找器从模拟快照中识别暗物质晕和次晕。

3. **星系-晕关联**：采用修改版的SciPic库，通过晕占据分布（HOD）框架在晕中生成星系。这提供了晕属性与星系统计量之间的模型无关映射。

4. **分析流程**：通过一个模型无关的分析流程处理模拟数据，计算成团性统计量。

5. **成团性分析**：通过以下方式研究星系成团性特征：
   - 红移空间两点相关函数（2PCF）的多极矩：$\xi_\ell(s)$，其中$\ell = 0,2,4,...$
   - VDG（基于Velocileptors的暗物质和星系成团性）：一种高性能的有效场论（EFT）模型，用于描述红移空间中的星系成团性，参数化了偏差和红移空间畸变。

6. **参数推断**：提取宇宙学参数，特别关注组合参数$f\sigma_{12}$，其中$f = d\ln D/d\ln a$是线性增长率，$\sigma_{12}$是半径为$12\ \mathrm{Mpc}/h$的球体内的物质密度涨落振幅。

7. **模板测试**：在分析不同基础模拟的数据时，使用各种宇宙学模型作为"模板"进行宇宙学参数推断，评估其稳健性和潜在偏差。

Result: 1. **Robustness of $f\sigma_{12}$**: The parameter combination $f\sigma_{12}$ exhibits notable robustness across a wide range of cosmological models when used as a cosmological template for inference. This extends previous findings to scenarios with markedly distinct gravitational or dark energy dynamics.

2. **Template-Induced Scatter**: Most of the scatter in cosmological parameter inference already appears when using the cosmological model of the simulations as the template (i.e., the "correct" template). Using a 'wrong' template introduces additional scatter, although with smaller amplitude compared to the intrinsic scatter from the correct template.

3. **Significant Deviations**: In many cases, deviations between inferred parameters from different templates are found to be much larger than the statistical error bars derived from the covariance. This suggests that the Gaussian approximation for the covariance matrix might be inadequate and requires further study for robust error estimation in Stage-IV surveys.

4. **Public Data Release**: The simulated galaxy catalogues from the broad suite of non-standard cosmological simulations are publicly released, providing a valuable resource for testing analysis pipelines and systematics.

5. **Implications for Future Surveys**: The results underscore that future cosmological investigations must broaden their scope beyond ΛCDM and rudimentary dynamical dark energy models to include a diverse array of non-standard theoretical frameworks to avoid template-induced biases.

主要结果：1. **$f\sigma_{12}$的稳健性**：当用作宇宙学推断的模板时，参数组合$f\sigma_{12}$在一系列广泛的宇宙学模型中表现出显著的稳健性。这一发现将先前的结果扩展到了具有显著不同引力或暗能量动力学的场景。

2. **模板引起的弥散**：宇宙学参数推断中的大部分弥散已经出现在使用模拟的宇宙学模型作为模板（即"正确"模板）时。使用"错误"模板会引入额外的弥散，但其幅度与正确模板的固有弥散相比更小。

3. **显著的偏离**：在许多情况下，发现不同模板推断出的参数之间的偏离远大于从协方差导出的统计误差。这表明协方差矩阵的高斯近似可能不充分，需要在第四代巡天中进行更深入的研究以实现稳健的误差估计。

4. **公开数据发布**：来自广泛非标准宇宙学模拟的模拟星系巡天目录已公开发布，为测试分析流程和系统误差提供了宝贵资源。

5. **对未来巡天的启示**：结果强调，未来的宇宙学研究必须将其范围扩展到ΛCDM和基本的动力学暗能量模型之外，以包含多样化的非标准理论框架，从而避免模板引起的偏差。

Conclusion: Stage-IV galaxy surveys like Euclid offer transformative potential for cosmology but require careful consideration of template assumptions in parameter inference. This work demonstrates that while the combined parameter $f\sigma_{12}$ shows remarkable robustness across diverse cosmological models, template mismatches can still introduce significant systematic errors that exceed statistical uncertainties. The public release of simulated catalogues for non-standard cosmologies provides essential tools for pipeline validation. Future analyses must incorporate broader theoretical priors and rigorously test covariance modeling assumptions, moving beyond Gaussian approximations to ensure robust constraints from next-generation surveys.

结论：以Euclid为代表的第四代星系巡天为宇宙学研究带来了变革性的潜力，但在参数推断中需要仔细考虑模板假设。本研究表明，尽管组合参数$f\sigma_{12}$在不同宇宙学模型中表现出显著的稳健性，但模板不匹配仍可能引入超过统计不确定性的显著系统误差。为非标准宇宙学公开发布的模拟目录为流程验证提供了必要工具。未来的分析必须纳入更广泛的理论先验，并严格检验协方差建模假设，超越高斯近似，以确保从下一代巡天中获得稳健的约束。

Abstract: Stage-IV galaxy surveys will provide the opportunity to test cosmological models and the underlying theory of gravity with unparalleled precision. In this context, it is crucial for the Euclid mission to leverage its spectroscopic and photometric probes to systematically investigate and incorporate non-standard cosmological models, including modified gravity, alternative dark energy scenarios, massive neutrinos, and primordial non-Gaussianity. We produce and release publicly simulated galaxy catalogues from a broad suite of non-standard cosmological simulations, which we processed through a model-independent analytical pipeline, making use of Rockstar for halo identification, and a modified version of the SciPic library for the galaxy-halo connection using the halo occupation distribution framework. We investigate their galaxy-clustering characteristics via the multipoles of the 2PCF in redshift space and VDG, a highly performant model for galaxy clustering. Across a wide range of models, the linear growth rate multiplied by the matter density within spheres of radius 12,Mpc, fs12, exhibits a notable robustness to the choice of cosmological template. Compared to previous works, our study extends this result to numerous scenarios with markedly distinct gravitational or dark energy dynamics. We find that the most of the scatter in cosmological parameter inference already appears when using the cosmological model of the simulations as templates. Using a `wrong' template can also introduce an additional scatter, although with smaller amplitude. Often, we find deviations much larger than error bars, meaning that the Gaussian approximation for the covariance might need to be further studied. Future cosmological investigations must broaden their scope to include a diverse array of non-standard theoretical frameworks, extending beyond LCDM and rudimentary dynamic dark energy models.

</details>


### [72] [Negative Masses and Spatial Curvature: Alleviating Neutrino Mass Tensions in LambdaCDM and Extended Cosmologies](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13208)
*Hayyim Pulido-Hernández,Jorge L. Cervantes-Cota*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: A joint analysis of CMB, BAO, and SNe Ia data reveals that spatial curvature and dynamical dark energy significantly impact neutrino mass constraints. The implementation of symmetric extensions to avoid boundary effects yields $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.011^{+0.052}_{-0.050}$ in $Λ$CDM+$Ω_k$+$\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$, reducing tension with terrestrial limits. More flexible models degrade precision but maintain consistency.

结合CMB、BAO和SNe Ia数据的联合分析表明，空间曲率和动力学暗能量显著影响中微子质量限制。为避免边界效应而实施的对称扩展方法在$Λ$CDM+$Ω_k$+$\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$框架下得到$\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.011^{+0.052}_{-0.050}$，减少了与地面极限的张力。更灵活的模型降低了精度但保持一致性。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The terrestrial lower limit on neutrino mass sum from oscillation experiments is $\sum m_ν \geq 0.06$ eV, while cosmological analyses under $\Lambda$CDM often prefer values consistent with zero, creating a $\sim 2.6\sigma$ tension. This tension could arise from physical degeneracies (e.g., with spatial curvature $Ω_k$) or methodological biases from physical boundaries. The motivation is to assess the robustness of cosmological $\sum m_ν$ bounds by exploring the impact of spatial curvature and dynamical dark energy while properly addressing boundary effects through symmetric extension techniques.

来自振荡实验的中微子质量和地面下限为$\sum m_ν \geq 0.06$ eV，而$\Lambda$CDM框架下的宇宙学分析通常倾向于接近零的值，产生了$\sim 2.6\sigma$的张力。这种张力可能源于物理简并性（如与空间曲率$Ω_k$的简并）或来自物理边界的方法学偏差。研究动机是通过探索空间曲率和动力学暗能量的影响，同时通过对称扩展技术正确处理边界效应，评估宇宙学$\sum m_ν$界限的稳健性。

Method: We perform a joint MCMC analysis using the latest cosmological data: CMB (Planck and ACT DR6), BAO (DESI DR2), and SNe Ia (DESY5 and DES-Dovekie). The key methodological innovation is the implementation of a symmetric extension wrapper for the neutrino mass parameter. Instead of imposing a hard physical boundary at $\sum m_ν = 0$, the technique allows sampling into the effectively negative mass region, preventing prior-driven biases near the boundary. This enables proper exploration of the posterior's behavior across the $\sum m_ν = 0$ threshold. Models considered include: $\Lambda$CDM + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$ (baseline), $\Lambda$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$, and $w_0 w_a$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$.

我们使用最新的宇宙学数据进行联合MCMC分析：CMB（Planck和ACT DR6）、BAO（DESI DR2）和SNe Ia（DESY5和DES-Dovekie）。关键的方法学创新是实现了中微子质量参数的对称扩展包装器。该方法不强制施加$\sum m_ν = 0$的硬物理边界，而是允许采样进入有效负质量区域，防止边界附近的先验驱动偏差。这使得能够正确探索$\sum m_ν = 0$阈值附近的后验行为。考虑的模型包括：$\Lambda$CDM + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$（基准）、$\Lambda$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$，以及$w_0 w_a$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$。

Result: 1. In $\Lambda$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$: $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.011^{+0.052}_{-0.050}$ eV, with the tension to the terrestrial limit reduced from $2.59\sigma$ (in $\Lambda$CDM + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$) to $1.17\sigma$. The posterior shows a smooth transition across $\sum m_ν = 0$, indicating the symmetric extension successfully mitigated boundary effects.

2. In the most flexible $w_0 w_a$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$: $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.07 \pm 0.11$ eV, with a tension of $1.13\sigma$. The increased parameter freedom significantly degrades the precision (uncertainty $\sim 0.11$ eV vs. $\sim 0.05$ eV in the simpler extension).

3. Spatial curvature $Ω_k$ is shown to be a primary source of degeneracy with $\sum m_ν$, modifying the posterior shape and shifting the preferred region.

1. 在$\Lambda$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$中：$\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.011^{+0.052}_{-0.050}$ eV，与地面极限的张力从$2.59\sigma$（在$\Lambda$CDM + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$中）降至$1.17\sigma$。后验分布在$\sum m_ν = 0$处显示平滑过渡，表明对称扩展成功缓解了边界效应。

2. 在最灵活的$w_0 w_a$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$中：$\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.07 \pm 0.11$ eV，张力为$1.13\sigma$。增加参数自由度显著降低了精度（不确定性$\sim 0.11$ eV vs. 较简单扩展中的$\sim 0.05$ eV）。

3. 空间曲率$Ω_k$被证明是与$\sum m_ν$简并的主要来源，改变了后验分布形状并移动了优选区域。

Conclusion: Current cosmological bounds on the neutrino mass sum $\sum m_ν$ are strongly affected by two factors: geometric degeneracies with spatial curvature $Ω_k$, and methodological biases from physical boundaries. The symmetric extension technique reveals that the $\sim 2.6\sigma$ tension between cosmological and terrestrial limits in the standard $\Lambda$CDM analysis largely dissipates ($\sim 1.2\sigma$) when allowing for spatial curvature and properly handling boundary effects. The degradation of precision in more complex models highlights the importance of model selection and parameter marginalization strategies. These findings suggest that claims of cosmological $\sum m_ν$ constraints must be interpreted with caution, considering both model flexibility and statistical methodology.

当前宇宙学对中微子质量和$\sum m_ν$的限制受到两个因素的强烈影响：与空间曲率$Ω_k$的几何简并性，以及来自物理边界的方法学偏差。对称扩展技术表明，当允许空间曲率并正确处理边界效应时，标准$\Lambda$CDM分析中宇宙学与地面极限之间的$\sim 2.6\sigma$张力大部分消散（$\sim 1.2\sigma$）。更复杂模型中精度的退化凸显了模型选择和参数边缘化策略的重要性。这些发现表明，在解释宇宙学$\sum m_ν$限制的声称时必须谨慎，需同时考虑模型灵活性和统计方法学。

Abstract: We investigate the impact of spatial curvature, $Ω_k$, and dynamical dark energy on the cosmological constraints of the neutrino mass sum, $\sum m_ν$. Using a joint analysis of the latest CMB (Planck and ACT DR6), BAO (DESI DR2) and SNe Ia (DESY5 and DES-Dovekie) datasets, we perform an exploration of the neutrino mass parameter space. To mitigate prior-driven biases near the physical boundary, we implement a symmetric extension wrapper that allows for effective negative masses. We find that the inclusion of spatial curvature significantly modifies the posterior distributions, exhibiting a smooth transition across the $\sum m_ν= 0$ threshold. In the $Λ$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$ framework, we obtain $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.011^{+0.052}_{-0.050}$, reducing the tension with the terrestrial lower limit of 0.06 eV from $2.59σ$ for the $Λ$CDM + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$ model to $1.17σ$. For the most flexible scenario $w_0 w_a$CDM + $Ω_k$ + $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}}$, we find $\sum m_{ν,\mathrm{eff}} = -0.07 \pm 0.11$ with a tension of $1.13σ$, illustrating how the increased parameter freedom notably degrades the precision of the mass estimate compared to simpler extensions. Our results demonstrate that current cosmological bounds on $\sum m_ν$ are heavily influenced by boundary effects and geometric degeneracies.

</details>


### [73] [Comparison of Cross-Correlation Methods for Line Intensity Mapping](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13218)
*Samuel H. Kramer,Patrick C. Breysse,Anthony R. Pullen,Faizah K. Siddique,Eric R. Switzer,Peter T. Timbie,Dongwoo Chung*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: Three cross-correlation techniques (stacking, CVID, cross power spectrum) applied to simulated [CII] LIM maps from EXCLAIM show signal detection at 4.5-8.4σ for current noise, improving to 24.6-44.0σ with reduced noise, enabling percent-level model constraints through combined analysis.

三种互相关技术(叠加、CVID、交叉功率谱)应用于EXCLAIM模拟[CII] LIM图显示当前噪声下4.5-8.4σ信号检测，在降低噪声条件下提升至24.6-44.0σ，通过组合分析实现百分比水平模型约束。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Line intensity mapping (LIM) provides 3D cosmological maps but many lines remain undetected due to foreground contamination and noise. Cross-correlation techniques offer the most robust path to detection and astrophysical constraint.

谱线强度映射(LIM)提供三维宇宙学图，但由于前景污染和噪声，许多谱线仍未探测。互相关技术提供最稳健的探测和天体物理约束路径。

Method: Applied three cross-correlation techniques: stacking, conditional voxel intensity distribution (CVID), and cross power spectrum to simulated [CII] LIM maps from EXCLAIM pathfinder experiment with realistic noise models. Analyzed redshift range 2.5-3.5.

应用三种互相关技术：叠加、条件体素强度分布(CVID)和交叉功率谱到EXCLAIM探路者实验的模拟[CII] LIM图，采用现实噪声模型。分析红移范围2.5-3.5。

Result: Detection significances: stacking 4.5σ, CVID 3.9σ, cross power spectrum 8.4σ for current noise levels. With reduced noise: 44.0σ, 24.6σ, 34.3σ respectively. Each technique provides unique information, with strongest constraints achieved through combined analysis.

探测显著性：当前噪声水平下叠加4.5σ、CVID 3.9σ、交叉功率谱8.4σ。降低噪声下：分别为44.0σ、24.6σ、34.3σ。每种技术提供独特信息，组合分析获得最强约束。

Conclusion: Cross-correlation techniques enable robust [CII] LIM detections even with significant contamination. The complementary nature of stacking, CVID, and power spectrum analysis provides powerful constraints on emission models when combined, with percent-level precision achievable in future low-noise scenarios.

互相关技术即使在显著污染条件下也能实现稳健的[CII] LIM探测。叠加、CVID和功率谱分析的互补性在组合时提供对发射模型的强大约束，未来低噪声场景下可实现百分比精度。

Abstract: Line intensity mapping (LIM) is a technique for producing 3D maps of the Universe by scanning the sky with a spectrometer sensitive to a range of wavelengths corresponding to the redshifted spectral lines of atoms or molecules, such as hydrogen or carbon, commonly found in galaxies and the diffuse media around them. While LIM experiments have successfully detected the 21 cm line of neutral hydrogen, other lines that reveal large-scale structure or astrophysical processes remain undetected. Many LIM experiments are in development or are underway to fill this gap, but will likely suffer from contamination from systematics, like Galactic foregrounds, or noise. Cross-correlation techniques offer the smoothest route for making detections and constraining astrophysical processes in this regime. In this work, we apply three cross-correlation techniques (stacking, the conditional voxel intensity distribution (CVID), and the cross power spectrum) to simulated LIM maps produced using [CII] luminosity models for a pathfinder LIM experiment (EXCLAIM). We find that these cross-correlation techniques allow for mean detection of the target signal line ([CII]) at redshifts 2.5-3.5 at the 4.5$σ$, 3.9$σ$, and 8.4$σ$ level, respectively, and offer moderate constraints on the line emission model. Under a futuristic scenario with reduced noise, the techniques improve substantially, with detections at the 44.0$σ$, 24.6$σ$, and 34.3$σ$ levels and percent-level constraints. Each technique offers unique information, with the strongest constraints achieved by using the three techniques in combination.

</details>


### [74] [A 2% determination of $N_{\rm eff}$ from primordial element abundance, cosmic microwave background, and baryon acoustic oscillation measurements](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.13226)
*Samuel Goldstein,J. Colin Hill*

Main category: astro-ph.CO

TL;DR: A new constraint on the effective number of relativistic degrees of freedom, $N_{\mathrm{eff}}=2.990\pm0.070$ (68% C.L.), is obtained by combining primordial helium and deuterium abundances, CMB data from $\it{Planck}$, ACT, and SPT, and BAO data from DESI. This is the tightest measurement to date and agrees with the Standard Model prediction of $N_{\mathrm{eff}}=3.044$. The excess contribution beyond three neutrino species is constrained to $\Delta N_{\mathrm{eff}}<0.107$ (95% C.L.), nearly reaching the minimum contribution from a light spin-3/2 particle decoupling after inflation. The analysis excludes large-scale $\it{Planck}$ polarization data for consistency, showing that $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ constraints are robust to optical depth uncertainties. These results impose stringent limits on light particles in the early universe and on models attempting to reconcile the Hubble tension.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Measuring $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$, the effective number of relativistic degrees of freedom in the early universe, provides a powerful probe of physics beyond the Standard Model (BSM). Precision constraints on $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ can reveal the presence of additional light particles (e.g., sterile neutrinos, axions, dark radiation) that were relativistic at the time of Big Bang Nucleosynthesis (BBN) and recombination. Furthermore, $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ impacts the expansion rate during these epochs, influencing light element abundances and CMB anisotropies. A precise determination of $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ also tests cosmological models that attempt to resolve the Hubble tension by introducing extra radiation density, as an increase in $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ can raise the CMB-inferred Hubble constant $H_0$. Recent advances in observational data, including improved primordial abundance measurements from the Large Binocular Telescope $Y_p$ Project, high-resolution CMB data from ACT and SPT, and large-scale BAO measurements from DESI, enable a more robust and independent constraint on $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$, minimizing systematic dependencies on large-scale CMB polarization (and thus the optical depth $\tau$) which can be degenerate with $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$.

Method: The analysis employs a Bayesian parameter inference framework using a comprehensive cosmological data combination. Key datasets include: (1) primordial helium abundance $Y_p$ from the Large Binocular Telescope $Y_p$ Project; (2) primordial deuterium abundance D/H from spectroscopic observations; (3) CMB temperature and polarization power spectra from $\it{Planck}$ (excluding large-scale polarization to avoid optical depth degeneracies), Atacama Cosmology Telescope (ACT), and South Pole Telescope (SPT); (4) baryon acoustic oscillation (BAO) measurements from the Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument (DESI). The cosmological model assumes a flat $\Lambda$CDM cosmology extended with $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ as a free parameter. The likelihood analysis incorporates the full covariance between datasets and accounts for relevant systematic uncertainties. The constraint on $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ is derived primarily from the combination of BBN (via $Y_p$ and D/H) and CMB/BAO data, which together break degeneracies with other parameters like the baryon density $\Omega_b h^2$ and the Hubble constant $H_0$. The analysis explicitly excludes $\it{Planck}$ large-scale polarization data to ensure consistency with ACT/SPT small-scale measurements and to demonstrate the robustness of $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ to $\tau$ priors.

Result: The combined analysis yields $N_{\mathrm{eff}} = 2.990 \pm 0.070$ (68% confidence level). This is the tightest constraint on $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ to date, with a precision of $\sim 2.3\%$. The result is in excellent agreement with the Standard Model prediction of $N_{\mathrm{eff}} = 3.044$ (accounting for non-instantaneous neutrino decoupling and QED corrections). The excess relativistic degrees of freedom beyond the three active neutrino species is constrained to $\Delta N_{\mathrm{eff}} < 0.107$ at 95% C.L. This bound approaches the theoretical minimum contribution of $\Delta N_{\mathrm{eff}} \approx 0.094$ from a light spin-3/2 particle that decoupled at any time after inflation ended. The analysis demonstrates that the inclusion or exclusion of $\it{Planck}$ large-scale polarization data (and thus constraints on the optical depth $\tau$) has negligible impact on the derived $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ value, indicating that $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ constraints are robust against uncertainties in $\tau$. The derived baryon density is $\Omega_b h^2 = 0.02237 \pm 0.00015$, consistent with independent BBN+CMB analyses.

Conclusion: The study presents the most precise measurement of $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ to date, strongly favoring the Standard Model value and placing stringent limits on additional light relativistic species in the early universe. The constraint $\Delta N_{\mathrm{eff}} < 0.107$ (95% C.L.) rules out many BSM scenarios that predict significant dark radiation, including certain sterile neutrino models and early dark energy models designed to address the Hubble tension. The near-saturation of the bound by the minimal contribution of a light spin-3/2 particle highlights the exceptional sensitivity of current cosmological data. The robustness of the $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$ constraint to the treatment of CMB optical depth $\tau$ resolves previous concerns about degeneracies and systematic uncertainties. These results significantly tighten the parameter space for light particle physics beyond the Standard Model and disfavor cosmological solutions to the Hubble tension that rely on increasing $N_{\mathrm{eff}}$. Future improvements will come from next-generation CMB experiments (CMB-S4, Simons Observatory) and spectroscopic surveys, potentially probing $\Delta N_{\mathrm{eff}} \sim 0.02$ and testing even more subtle deviations from the Standard Model.

Abstract: We present a new constraint on the effective number of relativistic species in the early universe, $N_{\rm eff}$, by combining recent primordial helium abundance measurements from the Large Binocular Telescope $Y_p$ Project with primordial deuterium abundance data, cosmic microwave background (CMB) observations from $\it{Planck}$, the Atacama Cosmology Telescope, and the South Pole Telescope, and baryon acoustic oscillation (BAO) data from the Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument, yielding $N_{\rm eff}=2.990\pm0.070$ (68% C.L.). This is the tightest constraint on $N_{\rm eff}$ to date, and is in excellent agreement with the standard model prediction of $N_{\rm eff}=3.044$. Furthermore, we constrain excess contributions to $N_{\rm eff}$ beyond the three neutrino species, finding $ΔN_{\rm eff}<0.107$ (95% C.L.). This bound nearly approaches the minimum contribution to $ΔN_{\rm eff}$ from a light spin-3/2 particle that decoupled at any time after inflation ended. Our baseline analysis does not include large-scale $\it{Planck}$ polarization information, enabling a fully consistent combination of state-of-the-art CMB and BAO measurements. As a byproduct, we show that current $N_{\rm eff}$ bounds are essentially insensitive to the inclusion or exclusion of optical depth constraints inferred from large-scale CMB polarization data, making $N_{\rm eff}$ highly robust in this regard. Our constraints place stringent limits on light particles in the early Universe and on a broad range of models aimed at increasing the CMB-inferred value of the Hubble constant.

</details>
